###xml 203 209 203 209 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93</italic>
###xml 230 235 230 235 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">e1500</italic>
###xml 299 305 299 305 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93</italic>
###xml 339 352 339 352 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93(e1500)</italic>
###xml 430 443 430 443 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93(e1500)</italic>
###xml 539 551 539 551 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1(n4588)</italic>
###xml 605 612 605 612 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-1000708-t005">Table 5</xref>
###xml 658 671 658 671 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93(e1500)</italic>
###xml 739 751 739 751 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1(n4588)</italic>
###xml 878 891 878 891 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93(e1500)</italic>
###xml 946 958 946 958 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sfa-1(n4562)</italic>
###xml 994 1001 994 1001 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-1000708-t005">Table 5</xref>
###xml 1029 1041 1029 1041 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1(n4588)</italic>
###xml 1059 1072 1059 1072 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93(e1500)</italic>
###xml 1159 1165 1159 1165 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93</italic>
###xml 1234 1246 1234 1246 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sfa-1(n4562)</italic>
###xml 1290 1303 1290 1303 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93(e1500)</italic>
###xml 1313 1325 1313 1325 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sfa-1(n4562)</italic>
###xml 1369 1382 1369 1382 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93(e1500)</italic>
###xml 1436 1449 1436 1449 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93(e1500)</italic>
###xml 1453 1465 1453 1465 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sfa-1(n4562)</italic>
###xml 1546 1552 1546 1552 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93</italic>
###xml 1558 1568 1558 1568 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s3">Discussion</xref>
To test whether uaf-1(n4588) could suppress the Unc phenotype of unc-93(e1500) independently of unc-93 splicing, we generated transgenic animals that overexpressed in the body-wall muscles a full-length unc-93 cDNA containing the e1500 gf mutation. Since this cDNA generates a fully spliced form of unc-93 mRNA, if alternative splicing of unc-93(e1500) accounted for the suppression of the rubberband Unc phenotype, overexpressed unc-93(e1500) cDNA would not generate an alternatively spliced isoform and the animals would be as Unc in an uaf-1(n4588) background as in a wild-type background. As shown in Table 5, in wild-type animals, overexpression of the unc-93(e1500) cDNA caused a strong rubberband Unc phenotype. The presence of the uaf-1(n4588) mutation reduced the severity of the rubberband Unc phenotype caused by the same transgenes. Similarly, overexpression of the unc-93(e1500) cDNA also caused a weaker rubberband Unc phenotype in sfa-1(n4562) animals than in wild-type animals (Table 5). This result implied that uaf-1(n4588) can suppress the unc-93(e1500) rubberband Unc phenotype through mechanism(s) other than by affecting the splicing of unc-93. This finding was consistent with our results showing that although sfa-1(n4562) suppressed the rubberband Unc phenotype of unc-93(e1500) animals, sfa-1(n4562) did not affect the alternative splicing of unc-93(e1500) exon 9, which also suggested that the suppression of unc-93(e1500) by sfa-1(n4562) was mediated by a mechanism other than by affecting the alternative splicing of unc-93 (see Discussion).
###end p 59
###begin title 60
###xml 0 12 0 12 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1(n4588)</italic>
###xml 17 29 17 29 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sfa-1(n4562)</italic>
###xml 106 119 106 119 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93(e1500)</italic>
uaf-1(n4588) and sfa-1(n4562) partially suppress the rubberband Unc phenotype caused by overexpression of unc-93(e1500) cDNA in body-wall muscles.
###end title 60
###begin p 61
###xml 29 35 29 35 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93</italic>
###xml 50 55 50 55 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">e1500</italic>
###xml 80 85 80 85 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">myo-3</sub>
###xml 75 109 75 109 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nEx[P<sub>myo-3</sub>unc-93(e1500) cDNA::gfp]</italic>
###xml 153 165 153 165 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1(n4588)</italic>
###xml 170 193 170 193 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sfa-1(n4562)/nT1[qIs51]</italic>
###xml 284 296 284 296 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1(n4588)</italic>
###xml 367 379 367 379 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sfa-1(n4562)</italic>
###xml 427 450 427 450 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sfa-1(n4562)/nT1[qIs51]</italic>
###xml 529 550 529 550 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
Transgenes that expressed an unc-93 cDNA with the e1500 missense mutation (nEx[Pmyo-3unc-93(e1500) cDNA::gfp]) in body-wall muscles were introduced into uaf-1(n4588) and sfa-1(n4562)/nT1[qIs51] animals, and four independent stable transgenic lines were established. Transgenes in the uaf-1(n4588) background were backcrossed into the wild-type background. Transgenic sfa-1(n4562) animals were obtained as progeny of transgenic sfa-1(n4562)/nT1[qIs51] animals. The locomotion of the transgenic animals was assayed as described in Materials and Methods. Comparison should be made between animals of either wild-type or mutant genotypes carrying the same transgenic extra-chromosomal array.
###end p 61
###begin p 62
###xml 22 45 22 45 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sfa-1(n4562)/nT1[qIs51]</italic>
"wild-type" refers to sfa-1(n4562)/nT1[qIs51], which exhibits a wild-type phenotype.
###end p 62
###begin title 63
Nucleotide substitutions at the intron 8 endogenous 3' splice site and the exon 9 cryptic 3' splice site alter the recognition of these two sites differently
###end title 63
###begin p 64
###xml 137 142 137 142 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1</italic>
###xml 224 231 224 231 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 371 384 371 384 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93(e1500)</italic>
###xml 412 421 412 421 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6A</xref>
###xml 507 513 507 513 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93</italic>
###xml 546 555 546 555 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6A</xref>
###xml 584 590 584 590 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93</italic>
###xml 710 719 710 719 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g004">Figure 4A</xref>
###xml 792 801 792 801 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6A</xref>
###xml 935 944 935 944 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6B</xref>
###xml 1043 1047 1043 1047 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000708-Hollins1">[29]</xref>
###xml 1049 1053 1049 1053 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000708-Blumenthal1">[63]</xref>
###xml 1054 1058 1054 1058 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000708-Zhang1">[65]</xref>
###xml 1107 1119 1107 1119 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6B&#8211;6E</xref>
The alternative splicing between the intron 8 endogenous 3' splice site (I8) and the exon 9 cryptic 3' splice site (E9) in wild-type and uaf-1 mutant animals allows an analysis of the effects of different nucleotides on the in vivo recognition of these alternatively spliced sites. We constructed a transgene that fuses the genomic sequence between exon 8 and exon 10 of unc-93(e1500) and the GFP reporter gene (Figure 6A) and placed the fusion transgene under the control of 2 kb of the promoter region of unc-93. We used a pair of PCR primers (Figure 6A, red arrows) that recognize unc-93 exon 8 and the GFP sequences to specifically amplify transgene cDNAs in RT-PCR experiments. The Taqman probes shown in Figure 4A were used to quantify the wild-type and alternatively spliced isoforms (Figure 6A). Because I8 and E9 have the same nucleotides at positions -3 to -1 (CAG), our mutagenesis analysis focused on nucleotides -7 to -4 (Figure 6B), which are variable and are known to be critical for recognition and binding by the U2AF complex [29], [63]-[65]. We named each of 16 transgene constructs 1-16 (Figure 6B-6E).
###end p 64
###begin title 65
###xml 163 175 163 175 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1(n4588)</italic>
Nucleotide substitutions at the intron 8 endogenous 3' splice site and the exon 9 cryptic 3' splice site affect splicing at these different sites in wild-type and uaf-1(n4588) animals.
###end title 65
###begin p 66
###xml 376 382 376 382 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93</italic>
###xml 407 419 407 419 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1(n4588)</italic>
###xml 750 762 750 762 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1(n4588)</italic>
###xml 1128 1140 1128 1140 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1(n4588)</italic>
(A) Exon structures of transgenes used for 3' splice site nucleotide substitution analysis. Location of PCR primers (red arrows) and Taqman probes (dark short lines) are indicated. (B-D) List of 3' splice site nucleotide substitutions and the proportion of alternatively spliced exon 9 expressed as a percentage of total spliced (wild-type and alternatively spliced products) unc-93 exon 9 in wild-type and uaf-1(n4588) animals carrying the corresponding transgenes. Nucleotide bases altered are in red, and bases that remain the same as in the original 3' splice site are in black. The designated positions (-7 to -1) of each base are indicated in transgene No. 1 of (B). For each transgene, two stable lines were established for both wild-type and uaf-1(n4588) animals, except in cases labeled with *, for which only one stable transgenic line was established. Each dataset represents the average value of duplicate measurements of each biological sample. Error bars: standard deviations. (E) Summary graph of the nucleotide substitution analysis shown in (B-D), indicating the % usage of each 3' splice site in wild-type and uaf-1(n4588) animals carrying the corresponding transgenes. -, 0 to 1%; +, 1 to 10%; ++, 10 to 30%; +++, 30 to 70%; ++++, 70 to 90%; +++++, 90 to 99%; ++++++, 99 to 100%.
###end p 66
###begin p 67
###xml 41 57 41 57 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6B and 6E</xref>
###xml 99 112 99 112 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93(e1500)</italic>
###xml 178 191 178 191 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93(e1500)</italic>
###xml 226 235 226 235 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6B</xref>
###xml 262 271 262 271 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g004">Figure 4B</xref>
###xml 316 328 316 328 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1(n4588)</italic>
###xml 379 388 379 388 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6B</xref>
###xml 414 427 414 427 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93(e1500)</italic>
###xml 508 517 508 517 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g004">Figure 4B</xref>
###xml 571 577 571 577 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93</italic>
###xml 640 647 640 647 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
We examined the splicing of a transgene (Figure 6B and 6E, No. 1) containing the same I8 and E9 as unc-93(e1500). In wild-type animals the splicing mimics that of the endogenous unc-93(e1500), with very little splicing at E9 (Figure 6B, 1.8%, compare to 1.3% in Figure 4B). Splicing of the same transgene (No. 1) in uaf-1(n4588) mutants occurred almost exclusively at E9 (>99%) (Figure 6B); endogenous splicing of unc-93(e1500) was qualitatively but not quantitatively similar, occurring mostly at E9 (68%) (Figure 4B). These results suggest that the splicing of mutated unc-93 transgenes could provide important information concerning the in vivo recognition of 3' splice sites.
###end p 67
###begin p 68
###xml 40 49 40 49 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6B</xref>
###xml 81 93 81 93 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1(n4588)</italic>
###xml 171 187 171 187 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6B and 6E</xref>
###xml 236 245 236 245 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6B</xref>
###xml 314 326 314 326 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1(n4588)</italic>
###xml 365 381 365 381 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6B and 6E</xref>
###xml 516 528 516 528 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1(n4588)</italic>
###xml 630 639 630 639 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6B</xref>
###xml 711 727 711 727 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6B and 6E</xref>
###xml 744 756 744 756 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1(n4588)</italic>
###xml 810 826 810 826 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6B and 6E</xref>
###xml 914 926 914 926 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1(n4588)</italic>
###xml 936 952 936 952 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6B and 6E</xref>
We replaced E9 with the sequence of I8 (Figure 6B, No. 2). In both wild-type and uaf-1(n4588) animals, splicing occurred mostly at the new E9 (97% and 98%, respectively) (Figure 6B and 6E). When I8 was replaced with the sequence of E9 (Figure 6B, No. 3), splicing again occurred mostly at E9 in both wild-type and uaf-1(n4588) animals (97% and >99%, respectively) (Figure 6B and 6E). These results suggest that the sequence that surrounds the original E9 is preferred by the splicing machinery in both wild-type and uaf-1(n4588) animals when two identical 3' splice sites are present. We next switched the positions of I8 and E9 (Figure 6B, No. 4). In the wild type most splicing (>99%) occurred at the new E9 (Figure 6B and 6E). Similarly, in uaf-1(n4588) animals, most splicing (80%) occurred at the new E9 (Figure 6B and 6E, No.4). However, that a significant amount of splicing (20%) occurred at the new I8 in uaf-1(n4588) animals (Figure 6B and 6E, No. 4) suggested that the mutant UAF-1 can efficiently recognize the original E9 sequence even at the I8 position, which is normally a less favorable position.
###end p 68
###begin p 69
###xml 84 88 84 88 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000708-Cramer1">[66]</xref>
###xml 90 96 90 96 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93</italic>
###xml 131 135 131 135 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000708-delaCruz1">[34]</xref>
###xml 136 140 136 140 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000708-Levin1">[37]</xref>
###xml 300 305 300 305 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">myo-3</italic>
###xml 315 319 315 319 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000708-Okkema1">[49]</xref>
###xml 321 337 321 337 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6B and 6E</xref>
###xml 422 427 422 427 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">myo-3</italic>
###xml 445 451 445 451 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93</italic>
###xml 462 478 462 478 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6B and 6E</xref>
###xml 550 563 550 563 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93(e1500)</italic>
The pattern of alternative splicing in cell culture can depend on the promoter used [66]. unc-93 is expressed in body-wall muscles [34],[37]. We tested whether a different muscle-specific promoter would alter the splicing pattern of transgene No. 1 by expressing the transgene under the control of a myo-3 promoter [49] (Figure 6B and 6E, No. 5). We found almost identical splicing patterns of the transgene driven by the myo-3 promoter and the unc-93 promoter (Figure 6B and 6E, compare No. 1 and No. 5), suggesting that the alternative splicing of unc-93(e1500) involves a mechanism that is not promoter-specific.
###end p 69
###begin p 70
###xml 75 85 75 85 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 119 123 119 123 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000708-Hollins1">[29]</xref>
###xml 125 129 125 129 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000708-Blumenthal1">[63]</xref>
###xml 130 134 130 134 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000708-Zhang1">[65]</xref>
###xml 215 227 215 227 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1(n4588)</italic>
###xml 237 253 237 253 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6C and 6E</xref>
###xml 403 412 403 412 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6C</xref>
###xml 507 511 507 511 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000708-Hollins1">[29]</xref>
###xml 512 516 512 516 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000708-Kent1">[64]</xref>
###xml 706 710 706 710 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000708-Hollins1">[29]</xref>
###xml 869 885 869 885 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6C and 6E</xref>
###xml 1029 1045 1029 1045 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6C and 6E</xref>
###xml 1315 1331 1315 1331 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6C and 6E</xref>
###xml 1613 1629 1613 1629 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6C and 6E</xref>
###xml 1658 1670 1658 1670 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1(n4588)</italic>
###xml 1717 1733 1717 1733 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6B and 6E</xref>
###xml 75 85 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
We examined the effects of base substitutions at I8. Replacing I8 with the C. elegans consensus 3' splice site TTTTcag [29], [63]-[65] caused splicing to occur exclusively (100%) at the new I8 in both wild-type and uaf-1(n4588) animals (Figure 6C and 6E, No. 6). To identify the nucleotides required for the recognition of I8 in wild-type animals, we substituted each base from -7 to -4 of I8 with a G (Figure 6C, No. 7 to No. 10). G is the least used nucleotide from -7 to -4 of identified 3' splice sites [29],[64] and in previous studies substituting T with G at any of the four bases from -7 to -4 of the highly consensus TTTTcag site significantly compromised binding of the U2AF complex to this site [29]. A G substitution at -7 (No. 7), -5 (No. 9) and -4 (No. 10) of I8 all dramatically reduced splicing at the new I8 (to the level of 15%, 0%, 0%, respectively; Figure 6C and 6E) in wild-type animals, suggesting that these nucleotides are critical for the recognition by wild-type UAF-1. However, a G substitution at -6 (Figure 6C and 6E, No. 8) did not cause a significant change of splicing at the new I8 (which is 96% compared to 98% of No. 1), suggesting this nucleotide is not essential for recognition by wild-type UAF-1. We also substituted the A at -6 with a C to generate an I8 more similar to E9 (Figure 6C and 6E, No. 11). Splicing at this I8 (No. 11) was similar to that of transgenes No. 1 and No. 8 in wild-type animals, consistent with the notion that this base is not essential for the recognition by wild-type UAF-1. For all the transgenes with single-base substitutions of I8, splicing (Figure 6C and 6E, No. 7, 8, 9, 10 and 11) in uaf-1(n4588) animals is similar to that of transgene No.1 (Figure 6B and 6E), suggesting that none of the substitutions significantly increased the affinity of I8 for mutant UAF-1.
###end p 70
###begin p 71
###xml 140 144 140 144 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000708-Hollins1">[29]</xref>
###xml 146 150 146 150 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000708-Blumenthal1">[63]</xref>
###xml 151 155 151 155 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000708-Zhang1">[65]</xref>
###xml 157 173 157 173 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6D and 6E</xref>
###xml 219 231 219 231 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1(n4588)</italic>
###xml 382 398 382 398 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6D and 6E</xref>
###xml 487 503 487 503 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6D and 6E</xref>
###xml 712 724 712 724 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1(n4588)</italic>
###xml 782 798 782 798 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6D and 6E</xref>
To test whether we could increase the recognition of E9, we replaced E9 with the highly conserved consensus 3' splice site TTTTcag sequence [29], [63]-[65] (Figure 6D and 6E, No. 12). As expected, in both wild-type and uaf-1(n4588) animals, splicing occurred exclusively at the new E9 (100% and 100%, respectively). We next changed each of the non-T bases to T from -7 to -4 of E9 (Figure 6D and 6E, No. 13, 14 and 15). A T at -7, -6 or -4 increased splicing at E9 in wild-type animals (Figure 6D and 6E, No. 13, 14 and 15)(53%, 100% and 91% for positions -7, -6 and -4, respectively), suggesting these substitutions increased recognition of E9 by wild-type UAF-1. For all three of these transgenes, splicing in uaf-1(n4588) animals occurred exclusively at E9 (100% for all three) (Figure 6D and 6E, No. 13, 14, and 15), suggesting none of the T substitutions significantly reduced the recognition of E9 by mutant UAF-1.
###end p 71
###begin p 72
###xml 38 54 38 54 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6D and 6E</xref>
###xml 146 167 146 167 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6B, 6D, and 6E</xref>
###xml 253 269 253 269 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6D and 6E</xref>
###xml 283 295 283 295 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1(n4588)</italic>
###xml 349 365 349 365 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6D and 6E</xref>
###xml 424 440 424 440 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000708-g006">Figure 6B and 6E</xref>
We mutated the C at -6 of E9 to an A (Figure 6D and 6E, No. 16), generating a 3' splice site with a T-to-G substitution at -4 of transgene No. 2 (Figure 6B, 6D, and 6E). Splicing of this transgene occurred exclusively at I8 (100%) in wild-type animals (Figure 6D and 6E, No. 16). In uaf-1(n4588) animals, splicing at the new E9 was reduced (to 62%, Figure 6D and 6E, No. 16) compared to that at E9 of transgene No. 2 (100%, Figure 6B and 6E, No. 2).
###end p 72

Discussion

###xml 1512 1524 1512 1524 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sfa-1(n4562)</italic>

###xml 1699 1712 1699 1712 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93(e1500)</italic>
###xml 1784 1790 1784 1790 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sup-10</italic>
###xml 1812 1824 1812 1824 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1(n4588)</italic>
###xml 1826 1838 1826 1838 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sup-10(n983)</italic>
###xml 1842 1854 1842 1854 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sfa-1(n4562)</italic>
###xml 1856 1868 1856 1868 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sup-10(n983)</italic>
###xml 1894 1906 1894 1906 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sup-10(n983)</italic>
###xml 1925 1937 1925 1937 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1(n4588)</italic>
###xml 1942 1954 1942 1954 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sfa-1(n4562)</italic>
###xml 2009 2015 2009 2015 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sup-10</italic>
###xml 2063 2068 2063 2068 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1</italic>
###xml 2073 2078 2073 2078 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sfa-1</italic>
###xml 2130 2143 2130 2143 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93(e1500)</italic>
###xml 2182 2195 2182 2195 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93(e1500)</italic>
###xml 2246 2251 2246 2251 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1</italic>
###xml 2256 2261 2256 2261 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sfa-1</italic>
###xml 2281 2294 2281 2294 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93(e1500)</italic>
###xml 2299 2311 2299 2311 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sup-10(n983)</italic>
###xml 2407 2420 2407 2420 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93(e1500)</italic>
###xml 2425 2437 2425 2437 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sup-10(n983)</italic>
###xml 2531 2544 2531 2544 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93(e1500)</italic>
###xml 2579 2592 2579 2592 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-93(e1500)</italic>
###xml 2596 2601 2596 2601 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1</italic>
The mechanism(s) of the suppression of the Unc phenotype caused by the unc-93(e1500) mutation by uaf-1(n4588) and sfa-1(n4562) remains to be determined. Four observations indicate that although uaf-1(n4588) causes alternative splicing of unc-93(e1500) exon 9, this alternative splicing is not the basis of the suppression. First, unc-93(e1500)/unc-93(lf) heterozygous animals are as Unc as unc-93(e1500) homozygous animals [36], indicating that reducing unc-93 expression by 50% does not reduce the rubberband Unc phenotype. By contrast, uaf-1(n4588 n5127) reduced unc-93(e1500) expression by 25% (since there was 25% alternative splicing), and these animals were strongly suppressed. Also, in uaf-1(n4588) unc-93(e1500) animals, the unc-93(e1500) transcript was reduced by 68% (there was 68% alternative splicing), and these animals might have been expected to be slightly less Unc than unc-93(e1500)/unc-93(lf) animals but instead were strongly suppressed. Thus, the level of reduction of the unc-93(e1500) transcript does not correlate with the level of the suppression of the unc-93(e1500) Unc phenotype by uaf-1(n4588 n5127) and uaf-1(n4588). Second, the strong rubberband Unc phenotype caused by overexpression of the unc-93(e1500)-specific cDNA in body-wall muscles was partially suppressed by uaf-1(n4588), suggesting that unc-93(e1500) splicing is not needed for uaf-1(n4588)-mediated suppression. Third, sfa-1(n4562) suppressed unc-93(e1500) without affecting the splicing of unc-93(e1500) exon 9, and sfa-1(n4562) partially suppressed the rubberband Unc phenotype caused by overexpression of the unc-93(e1500) cDNA in the body-wall muscles. Again, suppression can occur without affecting unc-93(e1500) mRNA splicing. Similarly, we did not identify an alternatively spliced sup-10 transcript in either uaf-1(n4588); sup-10(n983) or sfa-1(n4562); sup-10(n983) animals, suggesting that sup-10(n983) was suppressed by uaf-1(n4588) and sfa-1(n4562) by a mechanism other than alternative splicing of the sup-10 transcript. Fourth, reducing the expression of uaf-1 and sfa-1 by RNAi suppressed the rubberband Unc phenotype of unc-93(e1500) but did not cause altered splicing of unc-93(e1500) exon 9. Based on these arguments, we propose that uaf-1 and sfa-1 mutations suppress unc-93(e1500) and sup-10(n983) by affecting the splicing of one or more unidentified genes required for the expression of the unc-93(e1500) and sup-10(n983) rubberband Unc phenotype. We cannot exclude the possibility that the alternative splicing of unc-93(e1500) contributed to the suppression of unc-93(e1500) by uaf-1 mutations.
###end p 75
###begin title 76
###xml 0 5 0 5 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">uaf-1</italic>
